|LOR - Laboratory Limit of Reporting||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#1 Insufﬁcient data to set a guideline value based on health considerations||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#2 Trigger value for prevention of foliar injury. Trigger value for moderately tolerant crops (i.e. lucerne, barley, sorghum)||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#3 for groundwater systems||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#4 To minimise bioclogging of irrigation equipment||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#5 Requires site-specific assessment||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#6 Not necessary||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#7 Escherichia coli should not be detected in any 100 mL sample of drinking water. If detected in drinking water, immediate action should be taken including investigation of potential sources of faecal contamination.||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#8 NHMRC Australian Drinking Water Guideline (Health) adopted||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#9 Based on no adverse effects on poultry expected. Dairy cattle upper limit of 2,400 mg/L is adopted.||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#10 Based on 'high' tolerance crops such as wheat, cotton, lucerne, barley, beets and rhodes grass.||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#11 Insufficient data available to derive trigger values for other species of cyanobacteria, with the exception of Microcystis. There is an increasing risk to livestock health when Microcystis exceeds 11,500 cells/mL.||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|#12 The Environmental Reference Standard (Victorian Government Gazette, 2021) outlines - 10 E. coli/100 mL (if no human faecal contamination sources identified).||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|\* For comparison between guidelines and laboratory results, a conversion factor of 4.43 has been applied to convert Nitrate (as N) to Nitrate (as NO₃⁻)||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|^ For comparison between guidelines and laboratory results, a conversion factor of 3.29 has been applied to Nitrite (as N) to convert to Nitrite (as NO2-)||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|\* For comparison between guidelines and laboratory results, a conversion factor of 1.215 has been applied to Ammonia (as N) to convert to Ammonia (as NH3)||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|'To calculate ammonia as NH₃ use multiplying factor of 1.214 x ammonia as N value.||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
|a National Institue of Water & Atmospheric Research, NIWA, Updating Nitrate Toxicity Effects on Freshwater Aquatic Species (NIWA, January 2013)||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||||
